Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\n     4→//! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\n     5→//! very verbose. But importing a lot of things that a program never uses isn't\n     6→//! good either. A balance needs to be struck.\n     7→//!\n     8→//! The *prelude* is the list of things that Rust automatically imports into\n     9→//! every Rust program. It's kept as small as possible, and is focused on\n    10→//! things, particularly traits, which are used in almost every single Rust\n    11→//! program.\n    12→//!\n    13→//! # Other preludes\n    14→//!\n    15→//! Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\n    16→//! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\n    17→//! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\n    18→//! also define their own preludes.\n    19→//!\n    20→//! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\n    21→//!\n    22→//! The difference between 'the prelude' and these other preludes is that they\n    23→//! are not automatically `use`'d, and must be imported manually. This is still\n    24→//! easier than importing all of their constituent components.\n    25→//!\n    26→//! # Prelude contents\n    27→//!\n    28→//! The items included in the prelude depend on the edition of the crate.\n    29→//! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\n    30→//! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\n    31→//! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`] and [`std::prelude::rust_2018`] re-export this prelude.\n    32→//! It re-exports the following:\n    33→//!\n    34→//! * <code>[std::marker]::{[Copy], [Send], [Sized], [Sync], [Unpin]}</code>,\n    35→//!   marker traits that indicate fundamental properties of types.\n    36→//! * <code>[std::ops]::{[Fn], [FnMut], [FnOnce]}</code>, and their analogous\n    37→//!   async traits, <code>[std::ops]::{[AsyncFn], [AsyncFnMut], [AsyncFnOnce]}</code>.\n    38→//! * <code>[std::ops]::[Drop]</code>, for implementing destructors.\n    39→//! * <code>[std::mem]::[drop]</code>, a convenience function for explicitly\n    40→//!   dropping a value.\n    41→//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[size_of], [size_of_val]}</code>, to get the size of\n    42→//!   a type or value.\n    43→//! * <code>[std::mem]::{[align_of], [align_of_val]}</code>, to get the\n    44→//!   alignment of a type or value.\n    45→//! * <code>[std::boxed]::[Box]</code>, a way to allocate values on the heap.\n    46→//! * <code>[std::borrow]::[ToOwned]</code>, the conversion trait that defines\n    47→//! Span,\n   239→        method_name: Ident,\n   240→        self_ty: Ty<'tcx>,\n   241→        self_ty_span: Span,\n   242→        expr_id: hir::HirId,\n   243→        pick: &Pick<'tcx>,\n   244→    ) {\n   245→        // Rust 2021 and later is already using the new prelude\n   246→        if span.at_least_rust_2021() {\n   247→            return;\n   248→        }\n   249→\n   250→        // These std::iter::repeat(\"'_\")\n   302→                            .take(counts.lifetimes)\n   303→                            .chain(std::iter::repeat(\"_\").take(\n   304→ Applicability::MachineApplicable,\n   340→            );\n   341→        });\n   342→    }\n   343→\n   344→    fn trait_path_or_bare_name(\n   345→        &self,\n   346→        span: Span,\n   347→        expr_hir_id: HirId,\n   348→        trait_def_id: DefId,\n   349→    ) -> String {\n   350→        self.trait_path(span, expr_hir_id, trait_def_id).unwrap_or_else(|| {\n   351→            let expr_hir_id: HirId, trait_def_id: DefId) -> Option<String> {\n   357→        let applicable_traits = self.tcx.in_scope_traits(expr_hir_id)?;\n   358→        let applicable_trait = applicable_traits.iter().find(|t| t.def_id == trait_def_id)?;\n   359→        if applicable_trait.import_ids.is_empty() {\n   360→            // The trait was declared within the module, we only need to use its name.\n   361→            return None;\n   362→        }\n   363→\n   364→        let import_items: Vec<_> = applicable_trait\n   365→            .import_ids\n   366→            .iter()\n   367→            .map(|&import_id| self.tcx.hir_expect_item(import_id))\n   368→            .collect();\n   369→\n   370→        // Find an identifier with which this trait was imported (note that `_` doesn't count).\n   371→        for item in import_items.iter() {\n   372→            let (_, kind) = item.expect_use();\n   373→            match kind {\n   374→                hir::UseKind::Single(ident) => {\n   375→                    if ident.name != kw::Underscore {\n   376→                        return Some(format!(\"{}\", ident.name));\n   377→                    }\n   378→                }\n   379→                hir::UseKind::Glob => return None, // Glob import, so just use its name.\n   380→                hir::UseKind::ListStem => unreachable!(),\n   381→            }\n   382→        }\n   383→\n   384→        // All that is left is `_`! We need to use the full path. It doesn't matter which one we\n   385→        // pick, so just take the first one.\n   386→        match import_items[0].kind {\n   387→            ItemKind::Use(path, _) => {\n   388→                Some(join_path_idents(path.segments.iter().map(|seg| seg.ident)))\n   389→            }\n   390→            _ => {\n   391→                span_bug!(span, \"unexpected item kind, expected a use: {:?}\", import_items[0].kind);\n   392→            }\n   393→        }\n   394→    }\n   395→\n   396→    /// Creates a string version of the `expr` that includes explicit adjustments.\n   397→    /// Returns the string and also a bool indicating whether this is a *precise*\n   398→    /// suggestion.\n   399→    fn adjust_expr(\n   400→        &self,\n   401→        pick: &Pick<'tcx>,\n   402→        expr: &hir::Expr<'tcx>,\n   403→        outer: Span,\n   404→    ) -> (String, bool) {\n   405→        let derefs = \"*\".repeat(pick.autoderefs);\n   406→\n   407→        let autoref = match    {\n                return;\n            }\n\n            // if it's an inherent `self` method (not `&self` or `&mut self`), it will take\n            // precedence over the `TryInto` impl, and thus won't break in 2021 edition\n            if pick.autoderefs == 0 && pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment.is_none() {\n                return;\n            }\n\n            // Inherent impls only require not relying on autoref and autoderef in order to\n            // ensure that the trait implementation won't be used\n            self.tcx.node_span_lint(\n                prelude_or_array_lint,\n                self_expr.hir_id,\n                self_expr.span,\n                |lint| {\n                    lint.primary_message(format!(\n                        \"trait method `{}` will become ambiguous in Rust {edition}\",\n                        segment.ident.name\n                    ));\n\n                    let sp = self_expr.span;\n\n                    let derefs = \"*\".repeat(pick.autoderefs);\n\n                    let autoref = match pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment {\n                        Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::Autoref { mutbl, .. }) => {\n                            mutbl.ref_prefix_str()\n                        }\n                        Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ToConstPtr) | None => \"\",\n                        Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ReborrowPin(mutbl)) => match mutbl {\n                            hir::Mutability::Mut => \"Pin<&mut \",\n                            hir::Mutability::Not => \"Pin<&\",\n                        },\n                    };\n                    if let Ok(self_expr) = self.sess().source_map().span_to_snippet(self_expr.span)\n                    {\n                        let mut self_adjusted =\n                            if let Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ToConstPtr) =\n                                pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment\n                            {\n                                format!(\"{derefs}{self_expr} as *const _\")\n                            } else {\n pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment\n                        {\n                            self_adjusted.push('>');\n                        }\n\n                        lint.span_suggestion(\n                            sp,\n                            \"disambiguate the method call\",\n                            format!(\"({self_adjusted})\"),\n                            Applicability::MachineApplicable,\n                        );\n                    } else {\n                        let self_adjusted = if let Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::ToConstPtr) =\n                            pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment\n                        {\n                            format!(\"{derefs}(...) as *const _\")\n                        } else {\n                            format!(\"{autoref}{derefs}...\")\n                        };\n                        lint.span_help(\n                            sp,\n                            format!(\"disambiguate the method call with `({self_adjusted})`\",),\n                        );\n                    }\n                },\n            );\n        } else {\n            // trait implementations require full disambiguation to not clash with the new prelude\n            // additions (i.e. convert from dot-call to fully-qualified call)\n            self.tcx.node_span_lint(\n                prelude_or_array_lint,\n                call_expr.hir_id,\n                call_expr.span,\n                |lint| {\n                    lint.primary_message(format!(\n                        \"trait method `{}` will become ambiguous in Rust {edition}\",\n                        segment.ident.name\n                    ));\n\n                    let sp = call_expr.span;\n                    let );\n\n                    let (self_adjusted, precise) = self.adjust_expr(pick, self_expr, sp);\n                    if precise {\n                        let args = args.iter().fold(String::new(),                          \", {}\",\n                                self.sess().source_map().span_to_snippet(span).unwrap()\n                            )\n                            .unwrap();\n                            string\n                        });\n\n                        lint.span_suggestion(\n                            sp,\n                            \"disambiguate the associated function\",\n                            format!(\n                                \"{}::{}{}({}{})\",\n                                trait_name,\n                                segment.ident.name,\n                                if let Some(args) = segment.args.as_ref().and_then(|args| self\n                                    .sess()\n                                    .source_map()\n                                    .span_to_snippet(args.span_ext)\n                                    .ok())\n                                {\n             );\n                    } else {\n                        lint.span_help(\n                            sp,\n                            format!(\n                                \"disambiguate the associated function with `{}::{}(...)`\",\n                                trait_name, segment.ident,\n                            ),\n                        );\n                    }\n                },\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub(super) fn lint_fully_qualified_call_from_2018(\n        &self,\n        span: Span,\n        method_name: Ident,\n        self_ty: Ty<'tcx>,\n        self_ty_span: Span,\n        expr_id: hir::HirId,\n        pick: &Pick<'tcx>,\n    ) {\n        // Rust 2021 and later is already using the new prelude\n        if span.at_least_rust_2021() {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // These are the fully qualified methods added to prelude in Rust 2021\n        if !matches!(method_name.name, sym::try_into | sym::try_from | sym::from_iter) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // No need to lint if method came from std/core, as that will now be in the prelude\n        if STDLIB_STABLE_CRATES.contains(&self.tcx.crate_name(pick.item.def_id.krate)) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        // For from_iter, check if the type actually implements FromIterator.\n        // If we know it does not, we don't need to warn.\n        if method_name.name == sym::from_iter {\n            if let Some(trait_def_id) = self.tcx.get_diagnostic_item(sym::FromIterator) {\n                let any_type = self.infcx.next_ty_var(span);\n                if !self\n                    .infcx\n                    .type_implements_trait(trait_def_id, [self_ty, any_type], self.param_env)\n                    .may_apply()\n                {\n                    return;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // No need to lint if this is an inherent method called on a specific type, like `Vec::foo(...)`,\n        // since such methods take precedence over trait methods.\n        if matches!(pick.kind, probe::PickKind::InherentImplPick) {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        self.tcx.node_span_lint(RUST_2021_PRELUDE_COLLISIONS, expr_id, span, |lint| {\n            lint.primary_message(format!(\n                \"trait-associated function `{}` will become ambiguous in Rust 2021\",\n                method_name.name\n            ));\n\n            // \"type\" refers to either a type or, more likely, a trait from which\n            // the associated function or method is from.\n            let container_id = pick.item.container_id(self.tcx);\n            let trait_path = self.trait_path_or_bare_name(span, expr_id, container_id);\n            let trait_generics = self.tcx.generics_of(container_id);\n\n            let trait_name =\n                if trait_generics.own_params.len() <= trait_generics.has_self as usize {\n                    trait_path\n                } else {\n                    let counts = trait_generics.own_counts();\n                    format!(\n                        \"{}<{}>\",\n                        trait_path,\n                        std::iter::repeat(\"'_\")\n                            .take(counts.lifetimes)\n                            .chain(std::iter::repeat(\"_\").take(\n \")\n                    )\n                };\n\n            let mut self_ty_name = self_ty_span\n                .find_ancestor_inside(span)\n                .and_then(|span| self.sess().source_map().span_to_snippet(span).ok())\n                .unwrap_or_else(|| self_ty.to_string());\n\n            // Get the number of generics the self type has (if an Adt) unless we can determine that\n            // the user has written the self type with generics already which we (naively) do by looking\n            // for a \"<\" in `self_ty_name`.\n            if                       .collect::<Vec<_>>()\n                                .join(\", \")\n                        );\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n            lint.span_suggestion(\n                span,\n                \"disambiguate the associated function\",\n                format!(\"<{} as {}>::{}\", self_ty_name, trait_name, method_name.name,),\n                Applicability::MachineApplicable,\n            );\n        });\n    }\n\n    fn trait_path_or_bare_name(\n        &self,\n        span: Span,\n        expr_hir_id: HirId,\n        trait_def_id: DefId,\n    ) -> String {\n        self.trait_path(span, expr_hir_id, trait_def_id).unwrap_or_else(|| {\n            let key = self.tcx.def_key(trait_def_id);\n            format!(\"{}\", key.disambiguated_data.data)\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn trait_path(&self, span: Span, expr_hir_id: HirId, trait_def_id: DefId) -> Option<String> {\n        let applicable_traits = self.tcx.in_scope_traits(expr_hir_id)?;\n        let applicable_trait = applicable_traits.iter().find(|t| t.def_id == trait_def_id)?;\n        if applicable_trait.import_ids.is_empty() {\n            // The trait was declared within the module, we only need to use its name.\n            return None;\n        }\n\n        let import_items: Vec<_> = applicable_trait\n            .import_ids\n            .iter()\n            .map(|&import_id| self.tcx.hir_expect_item(import_id))\n            .collect();\n\n        // Find an identifier with which this trait was imported (note that `_` doesn't count).\n        for item in import_items.iter() {\n            let (_, kind) = item.expect_use();\n            match kind {\n                hir::UseKind::Single(ident) => {\n                    if ident.name != kw::Underscore {\n                        return Some(format!(\"{}\", ident.name));\n                    }\n                }\n                hir::UseKind::Glob => return None, // Glob import, so just use its name.\n                hir::UseKind::ListStem => unreachable!(),\n            }\n        }\n\n        // All that is left is `_`! We need to use the full path. It doesn't matter which one we\n        // pick, so just take the first one.\n        match import_items[0].kind {\n            ItemKind::Use(path, _) => {\n                Some(join_path_idents(path.segments.iter().map(|seg| seg.ident)))\n            }\n            _ => {\n                span_bug!(span, \"unexpected item kind, expected a use: {:?}\", import_items[0].kind);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a string version of the `expr` that includes explicit adjustments.\n    /// Returns the string and also a bool indicating whether this is a *precise*\n    /// suggestion.\n    fn adjust_expr(\n        &self,\n        pick: &Pick<'tcx>,\n        expr: &hir::Expr<'tcx>,\n        outer: Span,\n    ) -> (String, bool) {\n        let derefs = \"*\".repeat(pick.autoderefs);\n\n        let autoref = match pick.autoref_or_ptr_adjustment {\n            Some(probe::AutorefOrPtrAdjustment::Autoref { mutbl, .. }) => t)).collect::<Vec<_>>()\n            );\n            let mut iter = ctxt.marks().into_iter().rev().peekable();\n            let mut result = None;\n            // Find the last opaque mark from the end if it exists.\n            while let Some(&(mark, transparency)) = iter.peek() {\n                if transparency == Transparency::Opaque {\n                    result = Some(mark);\n                    iter.next();\n                } else {\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n            debug!(\n                \"resolve_crate_root: found opaque mark {:?} {:?}\",\n                result,\n                result.map(|r| r.expn_data())\n            );\n            // Then find the last semi-opaque mark from the end if it exists.\n            for (mark, transparency) in iter {\n                if transparency == Transparency::SemiOpaque {\n                    result = Some(mark);\n                } else {\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n            debug!(\n                \"resolve_crate_root: found semi-opaque mark {:?} {:?}\",\n                result,\n                result.map(|r| r.expn_data())\n            );\n            result\n        } else {\n            debug!(\"resolve_crate_root: not DollarCrate\");\n            ctxt = ctxt.normalize_to_macros_2_0();\n            ctxt.adjust(ExpnId::root())\n        };\n        let module = match mark {\n            Some(def) => self.expn_def_scope(def),\n            None => {\n                debug!(\n                    \"resolve_crate_root({:?}): found no mark (ident.span = {:?})\",\n                    ident, ident.span\n                );\n                return self.graph_root;\n            }\n        };\n        let module = self.expect_module(\n            module.opt_def_id().map_or(LOCAL_CRATE, |def_id| def_id.krate).as_def_id(),\n        );\n        debug!(\n            \"resolve_crate_root({:?}): got module {:?} ({:?}) (ident.span = {:?})\",\n            ident,\n            module,\n            module.kind.name(),\n            ident.span\n        );\n        module\n    }\n\n    fn resolve_self(&self, ctxt: &mut SyntaxContext,
